This is information conceptually \"passed down\"\n    53→ * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \"are we parsing strict code?\", and so\n    54→ * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\n    55→ *\n    56→ * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is information conceptually\n    57→ * \"returned up\" from parsing sub-nodes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\n    66→ * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\n    67→ * can be optimized away.\n    68→ *\n    69→ * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\n    70→ * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\n    71→ * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. This is information conceptually\n * \"returned up\" from parsing sub-nodes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\n * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\n * can be optimized away.\n *\n * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\n * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\n * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\n * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\n * constructor's arguments).\n * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\n * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\n * further into the parse tree. You may push to this stack via calling the\n * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\n * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\n * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\n *\n * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\n *\n * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \"pass-down\"\n * data and some \"return-up\" data.\n *\n * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\n * of itself (nestables inside nestables). Note you also push/pop to these via\n * passing `Parser->pc`, which the constructor of the sub-nestable knows which\n * ParseContext field to push to. The sub-nestables are:\n *\n * ParseContext::Statement: stack of statements.\n * `if (x) { while (true) { try { ..stack of [if, while, try].. } ... } }`\n *\n * ParseContext::LabelStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for labeled\n * statements, for e.g. `label: while (true) { break label; }`\n *\n * ParseContext::ClassStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for classes\n * the parser is currently inside of.\n *\n * ParseContext::Scope: Set of variables in each scope (stack of sets):\n * `{ let a; let b; { let c; } }`\n * (this gets complicated with `var`, etc., check the class for docs)\n */\n\nclass JSFunction;\nclass JSObject;\nclass JSScript;\nstruct JSContext;\n\nnamespace js {\n\nclass ModuleObject;\nclass FrontendContext;\nclass Scope;\n\nnamespace frontend Certain limitations of\n * C++ (primarily the inability to partially specialize function templates),\n * plus the desire to minimize compiled code size in duplicate function\n * template instantiations wherever possible, mean that Parser exhibits much of\n * the same unholy template/inheritance complexity as token streams.\n *\n * == ParserSharedBase ==\n *\n * ParserSharedBase is the base class for both regular JS and BinAST parsing.\n * This class contains common fields and methods between both parsers. There is\n * currently no BinAST parser here so this can potentially be merged into the\n * ParserBase type below.\n *\n * == ParserBase → ParserSharedBase, ErrorReportMixin ==\n *\n * ParserBase is the base class for regular JS parser, shared by all regular JS\n * parsers of all character types and parse-handling behavior.  It stores\n * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\n *\n * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\n * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\n * character-type-agnostic.  The character-type-sensitive components residing\n * in |TokenStreamSpecific| (see the comment near the top of TokenStream.h)\n * live elsewhere in this hierarchy. Such functionality is implemented\n * through functions in PerHandlerParser.\n *\n * Functionality only used by syntax parsing or full parsing doesn't live here:\n * it should be implemented in the appropriate Parser<ParseHandler> (described\n * further below).\n *\n * == GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> → PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> ==\n *\n * Most parsing behavior varies across the character-type axis (and possibly\n * along the full/syntax axis). sequence, and related stencil data.\n    88→//\n    89→// BytecodeEmitter can be nested, in order to emit inner non-lazy function\n    90→// scripts.\n    91→//\n    92→//\n    93→// Bytecode JavaScript parsing and compilation to bytecode chain in Firefox is orchestrated through the following components:\\n\\n## Entry Point: BytecodeCompiler\\nThe compilation process begins in `js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.cpp` with the `CompileGlobalScriptToStencilAndMaybeInstantiate()` function. This is the high-level driver that coordinates the entire parsing and bytecode generation pipeline.\\n\\n## Tokenization: TokenStream\\nBefore parsing begins, the source text is tokenized using `TokenStream` (js/src/frontend/TokenStream.h and TokenStream.cpp). The TokenStream classes are split into `TokenStreamAnyChars` (character-type agnostic) and `TokenStreamSpecific` (character-type sensitive) components. The token stream reads and matches tokens from the source buffer.\\n\\n## Parser: AST Generation\\nThe parser (js/src/frontend/Parser.h and Parser.cpp) is instantiated through a template-based hierarchy:\\n- `ParserBase`: Base class shared across all JS parsers\\n- `GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit>`: Template-specialized for character type and handler type\\n- `Parser<ParseHandler, Unit>`: Final implementation\\n\\nThe parser generates an Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) by calling functions like `Parser::globalBody()` or `Parser::evalBody()` which return `ParseNode` objects.\\n\\n## AST Node Types: ParseNode\\nAST nodes are defined in `js/src/frontend/ParseNode.h` and ParseNode.cpp. The ParseNode hierarchy includes:\\n- `NullaryNode`: No children\\n- `UnaryNode`: One child\\n- `BinaryNode`: Two children  \\n- `TernaryNode`: Three children\\n- `ListNode`: Variable number of children\\n- Specialized nodes like `FunctionNode`, `ModuleNode`, `NameNode`, `NumericLiteral`, etc.\\n\\nThe complete set of ParseNode kinds is defined in the FOR_EACH_PARSE_NODE_KIND macro.\\n\\n## Bytecode Emitter: Bytecode Generation\\nOnce the AST is created, the `BytecodeEmitter` (js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.h and BytecodeEmitter.cpp) traverses the AST and emits bytecode instructions. The emitter:\\n- Receives the ParseNode tree\\n- Generates bytecode sequences stored in `BytecodeSection`\\n- Collects GC thing references in `PerScriptData`\\n- Tracks jump locations and control flow\\n- Manages scopes and bindings via `EmitterScope`\\n\\nThe main entry point is `BytecodeEmitter::emitScript()` which processes the top-level AST.\\n\\n## Stencil Intermediate Format\\nThe parsed and emitted data is stored in a `CompilationStencil` (js/src/frontend/Stencil.h and Stencil.cpp) before GC instantiation. The stencil format includes:\\n- `ScriptStencil`: Per-script bytecode and metadata\\n- `ScriptStencilExtra`: Additional script properties\\n- Atoms, scopes, and GC object references\\n- This intermediate format allows for caching, serialization, and off-thread compilation\\n\\n## JSScript Bytecode Output\\nThe final bytecode is materialized into a `JSScript` object (js/src/vm/JSScript.h and JSScript.cpp) through:\\n- `JSScript::Create()`: Creates the JSScript heap object\\n- `JSScript::fromStencil()`: Converts a CompilationStencil into a JSScript with actual bytecode\\n- `fullyInitFromStencil()`: Initializes all fields from the stencil\\n\\nThe JSScript contains:\\n- Bytecode instructions (sequence of jsbytecode)\\n- GC references to objects, strings, and functions\\n- Script metadata (flags, extents, scope information)\\n- Exception handling and try-note data\\n\\n## Opcodes\\nThe bytecode operations are defined in `js/src/vm/Opcodes.h` and use the JSOp enum. Each operation (like JSOP_ADD, JSOP_CALL, JSOP_RETURN) represents a single bytecode instruction that the interpreter executes.\\n\\n## Overall Flow Summary\\nThe complete compilation pipeline is:\\n1. Source text → TokenStream (tokenization)\\n2. Tokens → Parser → ParseNode (AST generation)\\n3. ParseNode → BytecodeEmitter → BytecodeSection (bytecode generation)\\n4. BytecodeSection → CompilationStencil (intermediate format)\\n5. CompilationStencil → JSScript (final bytecode object)\\n\\nThe `ScriptCompiler` class in BytecodeCompiler.cpp orchestrates this entire process, while helper emitters (`AsyncEmitter`, `FunctionEmitter`, `ClassEmitter`, etc.) handle specific language features. The bytecode is ultimately executed by the SpiderMonkey interpreter or JIT compiler.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":347,"cache_read_input_tokens":58479,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":347},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"d1aae417-3890-47c1-9815-a904c7626c4c","uuid":"abf3c408-c075-47d3-91c1-658c4f1cf825"}

The token stream reads and matches tokens from the source buffer.\\n\\n## Parser: AST Generation\\nThe parser (js/src/frontend/Parser.h and Parser.cpp) is instantiated through a template-based hierarchy:\\n- `ParserBase`: Base class shared across all JS parsers\\n- `GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit>`: Template-specialized for character type and handler type\\n- `Parser<ParseHandler, Unit>`: Final implementation\\n\\nThe parser generates an Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) by calling functions like `Parser::globalBody()` or `Parser::evalBody()` which return `ParseNode` objects.\\n\\n## AST Node Types: ParseNode\\nAST nodes are defined in `js/src/frontend/ParseNode.h` and ParseNode.cpp. The ParseNode hierarchy includes:\\n- `NullaryNode`: No children\\n- `UnaryNode`: One child\\n- `BinaryNode`: Two children  \\n- `TernaryNode`: Three children\\n- `ListNode`: Variable number of children\\n- Specialized nodes like `FunctionNode`, `ModuleNode`, `NameNode`, `NumericLiteral`, etc.\\n\\nThe complete set of ParseNode kinds is defined in the FOR_EACH_PARSE_NODE_KIND macro.\\n\\n## Bytecode Emitter: Bytecode Generation\\nOnce the AST is created, the `BytecodeEmitter` (js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.h and BytecodeEmitter.cpp) traverses the AST and emits bytecode instructions. The stencil format includes:\\n- `ScriptStencil`: Per-script bytecode and metadata\\n- `ScriptStencilExtra`: Additional script properties\\n- Atoms, scopes, and GC object references\\n- This intermediate format allows for caching, serialization, and off-thread compilation\\n\\n## JSScript Bytecode Output\\nThe final bytecode is materialized into a `JSScript` object (js/src/vm/JSScript.h and JSScript.cpp) through:\\n- `JSScript::Create()`: Creates the JSScript heap object\\n- `JSScript::fromStencil()`: Converts a CompilationStencil into a JSScript with actual bytecode\\n- `fullyInitFromStencil()`: Initializes all fields from the stencil\\n\\nThe JSScript contains:\\n- Bytecode instructions (sequence of jsbytecode)\\n- GC references to objects, strings, and functions\\n- Script metadata (flags, extents, scope information)\\n- Exception handling and try-note data\\n\\n## Opcodes\\nThe bytecode operations are defined in `js/src/vm/Opcodes.h` and use the JSOp enum. Each operation (like JSOP_ADD, JSOP_CALL, JSOP_RETURN) represents a single bytecode instruction that the interpreter executes.\\n\\n## Overall Flow Summary\\nThe complete compilation pipeline is:\\n1. Source text → TokenStream (tokenization)\\n2. Tokens → Parser → ParseNode (AST generation)\\n3. ParseNode → BytecodeEmitter → BytecodeSection (bytecode generation)\\n4. BytecodeSection → CompilationStencil (intermediate format)\\n5. CompilationStencil → JSScript (final bytecode object)\\n\\nThe `ScriptCompiler` class in BytecodeCompiler.cpp orchestrates this entire process, while helper emitters (`AsyncEmitter`, `FunctionEmitter`, `ClassEmitter`, etc.) handle specific language features. The bytecode is ultimately executed by the SpiderMonkey interpreter or JIT compiler.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
